<p><b>Rabindranath Tagore</b> <span class="noexcerpt nowraplinks" style="font-size:85%; font-weight:normal;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fellows_of_The_Royal_Asiatic_Society_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="Fellows of The Royal Asiatic Society of Great Britain and Ireland">FRAS</a></span> (<span class="rt-commentedText title="/É/: 'a' in 'about'">É</span><span title="/Ë/: primary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="/Éª/: 'i' in 'kit'">Éª</span><span title="'n' in style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tagor.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a>: <span lang="bn">à¦°à¦¬à§à¦¨à§à¦¦à§à¦°à¦¨à¦¾à¦¥ à¦ à¦¾à¦à§à¦°</span>; 7 May 1861Â â 7 August 1941) was a <a href="/wiki/Bengalis" title="Bengalis">Bengali</a> <a href="/wiki/Polymath" title="Polymath">polymath</a> who worked as a poet, writer, playwright, composer, philosopher, social reformer and painter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stern2001_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stern2001-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Henry_Newman_1921_252_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Henry_Newman_1921_252-3">[3]</a></sup> He reshaped <a href="/wiki/Bengali_literature" title="Bengali literature">Bengali literature</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Bengal" title="Music of Bengal">music</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Indian_art" title="Indian art">Indian art</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contextual_Modernism" title="Contextual Modernism">Contextual Modernism</a> in the late 19th and early 20th centuries. Author of the "profoundly sensitive, fresh and beautiful" poetry of <i><a href="/wiki/Gitanjali" title="Gitanjali">Gitanjali</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Nobel_Foundation_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Nobel_Foundation-4">[4]</a></sup> he became in 1913 the first non-European and the first lyricist to win the <a href="/wiki/1913_Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="1913 Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEO'Connell2008_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO'Connell2008-5">[5]</a></sup> Tagore's poetic songs were viewed as spiritual and mercurial; however, his "elegant prose and magical poetry" remain largely unknown outside Bengal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESen1997_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESen1997-6">[6]</a></sup> He was a fellow of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Asiatic_Society_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="Royal Asiatic Society of Great Britain and Ireland">Royal Asiatic Society</a>. Referred to as "the <a href="/wiki/Bard" title="Bard">Bard</a> of Bengal",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stern2001_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Stern2001-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Henry_Newman_1921_252_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Henry_Newman_1921_252-3">[3]</a></sup> Tagore was known by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sobriquets" title="Sobriquets">sobriquets</a>: <b>Gurudev</b>, <b>Kobiguru</b>, <b>Biswakobi</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[a]</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Brahmin" title="Bengali Brahmin">Bengali Brahmin</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Calcutta" title="Calcutta">Calcutta</a> with ancestral <a href="/wiki/Zamindar" title="Zamindar">gentry</a> roots in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burdwan_district" title="Burdwan district">Burdwan district</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tagore1_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-tagore1-10">[9]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Jessore_District" title="Jessore District">Jessore</a>, Tagore wrote poetry as an eight-year-old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETagore1984xii_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETagore1984xii-11">[10]</a></sup> At the age of sixteen, he released <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bh%C4%81nusi%E1%B9%83ha_%E1%B9%ACh%C4%81kurer_Pa%E1%B8%8D%C4%81val%C4%AB" title="BhÄnusiá¹ha á¹¬hÄkurer Paá¸ÄvalÄ«">his first substantial poems</a> under the pseudonym <i>BhÄnusiá¹ha</i> ("Sun Lion"), which were seized upon by literary authorities as long-lost classics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThompson192627â28Dasgupta199320_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThompson192627â28Dasgupta199320-12">[11]</a></sup> By 1877 he graduated to his first short stories and dramas, published under his real name. As a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humanist" title="Humanist">humanist</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universalist" title="Universalist">universalist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internationalism_(politics)" title="Internationalism (politics)">internationalist</a>, and ardent critic of <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup> he denounced the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British Raj</a> and advocated independence from Britain. As an exponent of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bengal_Renaissance" title="Bengal Renaissance">Bengal Renaissance</a>, he advanced a vast canon that comprised paintings, sketches and doodles, hundreds of texts, and some two thousand songs; his legacy also endures in his founding of <a href="/wiki/Visva-Bharati_University" title="Visva-Bharati University">Visva-Bharati University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDatta20022Kripalani2005a6â8Kripalani2005b2â3Thompson192612_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDatta20022Kripalani2005a6â8Kripalani2005b2â3Thompson192612-15">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tagore modernised Bengali art by spurning rigid classical forms and resisting linguistic strictures. His novels, stories, songs, dance-dramas, and essays spoke to topics political and personal. <i><a href="/wiki/Gitanjali" title="Gitanjali">Gitanjali</a></i> (<i>Song Offerings</i>), <i><a href="/wiki/Gora_(novel)" title="Gora (novel)">Gora</a></i> (<i>Fair-Faced</i>) and <i>Ghare-Baire</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Home_and_the_World" title="The Home and the World">The Home and the World</a></i>) are his best-known works, and his verse, short stories, and novels were acclaimedâor pannedâfor their lyricism, colloquialism, naturalism, and unnatural contemplation. His compositions were chosen by two nations as national anthems: India's "<a href="/wiki/Jana_Gana_Mana" title="Jana Gana Mana">Jana Gana Mana</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>'s "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amar_Shonar_Bangla" title="Amar Shonar Bangla">Amar Shonar Bangla</a>". The <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka_Matha" title="Sri Lanka Matha">Sri Lankan national anthem</a> was inspired by his work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RB1_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-RB1-16">[15]</a></sup>
</p>
